  <h3>
    <svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-book" height="16" version="1.1" viewBox="0 0 16 16" width="16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M3 5h4v1H3V5zm0 3h4V7H3v1zm0 2h4V9H3v1zm11-5h-4v1h4V5zm0 2h-4v1h4V7zm0 2h-4v1h4V9zm2-6v9c0 .55-.45 1-1 1H9.5l-1 1-1-1H2c-.55 0-1-.45-1-1V3c0-.55.45-1 1-1h5.5l1 1 1-1H15c.55 0 1 .45 1 1zm-8 .5L7.5 3H2v9h6V3.5zm7-.5H9.5l-.5.5V12h6V3z"></path></svg>
    README.md
  </h3>

    <article class="markdown-body entry-content" itemprop="text"><h1><a href="#capybara" aria-hidden="true" class="anchor" id="user-content-capybara"><svg aria-hidden="true" class="octicon octicon-link" height="16" version="1.1" viewBox="0 0 16 16" width="16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Capybara</h1>

    <p><a href=“travis-ci.org/teamcapybara/capybara”> src=“camo.githubusercontent.com/d2a69513271c0ce3ff12368f5ea3fa02d453b835/68747470733a2f2f7365637572652e7472617669732d63692e6f72672f7465616d63617079626172612f63617079626172612e737667” alt=“Build Status” data-canonical-src=“secure.travis-ci.org/teamcapybara/capybara.svg” style=“max-width:100%;”></a> <a href=“gemnasium.com/teamcapybara/capybara”> src=“camo.githubusercontent.com/c5284aecafa9fab95a241b126a60c6c42619d552/68747470733a2f2f67656d6e617369756d2e636f6d2f7465616d63617079626172612f63617079626172612e737667” alt=“Dependency Status” data-canonical-src=“gemnasium.com/teamcapybara/capybara.svg” style=“max-width:100%;”></a> <a href=“codeclimate.com/github/teamcapybara/capybara”> src=“camo.githubusercontent.com/4565053fa187f1cd5538143f10510f2aa65c022f/68747470733a2f2f636f6465636c696d6174652e636f6d2f6769746875622f7465616d63617079626172612f63617079626172612e737667” alt=“Code Climate” data-canonical-src=“codeclimate.com/github/teamcapybara/capybara.svg” style=“max-width:100%;”></a> <a href=“gitter.im/jnicklas/capybara?utm_source=badge&utm_medium=badge&utm_campaign=pr-badge&utm_content=badge”> src=“camo.githubusercontent.com/da2edb525cde1455a622c58c0effc3a90b9a181c/68747470733a2f2f6261646765732e6769747465722e696d2f4a6f696e253230436861742e737667” alt=“Gitter” data-canonical-src=“badges.gitter.im/Join%20Chat.svg” style=“max-width:100%;”></a></p> <p>Capybara helps you test web applications by simulating how a real user would interact with your app. It is agnostic about the driver running your tests and comes with Rack::Test and Selenium support built in. WebKit is supported through an external gem.</p> <h2><a href=“#support-capybara” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-support-capybara”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a>Support Capybara</h2> <p>If you and/or your company find value in Capybara and would like to contribute financially to its ongoing maintenance and development, please visit <a href=“Patreonwww.patreon.com/capybara”>Patreon> <p><strong>Need help?</strong> Ask on the mailing list (please do not open an issue on GitHub): <a href=“#finding”>Finding</a></li> <li><a href=“#scoping”>Scoping</a></li> <li><a href=“#working-with-windows”>Working with windows</a></li> <li><a href=“#scripting”>Scripting</a></li> <li><a href=“#modals”>Modals</a></li> <li><a href=“#debugging”>Debugging</a></li> </ul> </li> <li><a href=“#matching”>Matching</a> <ul> <li><a href=“#exactness”>Exactness</a></li> <li><a href=“#strategy”>Strategy</a></li> </ul> </li> <li><a href=“#transactions-and-database-setup”>Transactions and database setup</a></li> <li><a href=“#asynchronous-javascript-ajax-and-friends”>Asynchronous JavaScript (Ajax and friends)</a></li> <li><a href=“#using-the-dsl-elsewhere”>Using the DSL elsewhere</a></li> <li><a href=“#calling-remote-servers”>Calling remote servers</a></li> <li><a href=“#using-sessions”>Using sessions</a></li> <li><a href=“#xpath-css-and-selectors”>XPath, CSS and selectors</a></li> <li><a href=“#beware-the-xpath–trap”>Beware the XPath // trap</a></li> <li><a href=“#configuring-and-adding-drivers”>Configuring and adding drivers</a></li> <li><a href=“#gotchas”>Gotchas:</a></li> <li><a href=“#threadsafe”>“Threadsafe” mode</a></li> <li><a href=“#development”>Development</a></li> </ul> <h2><a href=“#key-benefits” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-key-benefits”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-key-benefits”></a>Key benefits</h2> <ul> <li><strong>No setup</strong> necessary for Rails and Rack application. Works out of the box.</li> <li><strong>Intuitive API</strong> which mimics the language an actual user would use.</li> <li><strong>Switch the backend</strong> your tests run against from fast headless mode to an actual browser with no changes to your tests.</li> <li><strong>Powerful synchronization</strong> features mean you never have to manually wait for asynchronous processes to complete.</li> </ul> <h2><a href=“#setup” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-setup”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-setup”></a>Setup</h2> <p>Capybara requires Ruby 1.9.3 or later. To install, add this line to your Gemfile and run bundle install:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>gem <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>capybara<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span></pre></div> <p><strong>Note:</strong> If using Ruby &lt; 2.0 you will also need to limit the version of rack to &lt; 2.0</p> <p>If the application that you are testing is a Rails app, add this line to your test helper file:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-k”>require</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>capybara/rails<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span></pre></div> <p><strong>Note:</strong> In Rails 4.0/4.1 the default test environment (config/environments/test.rb) is <a href=“not”>github.com/rails/rails/issues/15089“>not threadsafe</a>. If you experience random errors about missing constants, add config.allow_concurrency = false to config/environments/test.rb.</p> <p>If the application that you are testing is a Rack app, but not Rails, set Capybara.app to your Rack app:</p> <div class=”highlight highlight-source-ruby“><pre><span class=”pl-c1“>Capybara</span>.app <span class=”pl-k“>=</span> <span class=”pl-c1“>MyRackApp</span></pre></div> <p>If you need to test JavaScript, or if your app interacts with (or is located at) a remote URL, you'll need to <a href=”#drivers“>use a different driver</a>. If using Rails 5.0+, but not using the Rails system tests from 5.1, you'll probably also want to swap the ”server“ used to launch your app to Puma in order to match Rails defaults.</p> <div class=”highlight highlight-source-ruby“><pre><span class=”pl-c1“>Capybara</span>.server <span class=”pl-k“>=</span> <span class=”pl-c1“>:puma</span> <span class=”pl-c“><span class=”pl-c“>#</span> Until your setup is working</span> <span class=”pl-c1“>Capybara</span>.server <span class=”pl-k“>=</span> <span class=”pl-c1“>:puma</span>, { <span class=”pl-c1“>Silent:</span> <span class=”pl-c1“>true</span> } <span class=”pl-c“><span class=”pl-c“>#</span> To clean up your test output</span></pre></div> <h2><a href=”#using-capybara-with-cucumber“ aria-hidden=”true“ class=”anchor“ id=”user-content-using-capybara-with-cucumber“><svg aria-hidden=”true“ class=”octicon octicon-link“ height=”16“ version=”1.1“ viewBox=”0 0 16 16“ width=”16“><path fill-rule=”evenodd“ d=”M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z“></path></svg></a><a name=”user-content-using-capybara-with-cucumber“></a>Using Capybara with Cucumber</h2> <p>The cucumber-rails gem comes with Capybara support built-in. If you are not using Rails, manually load the capybara/cucumber module:</p> <div class=”highlight highlight-source-ruby“><pre><span class=”pl-k“>require</span> <span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>capybara/cucumber<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span> <span class=”pl-c1“>Capybara</span>.app <span class=”pl-k“>=</span> <span class=”pl-c1“>MyRackApp</span></pre></div> <p>You can use the Capybara DSL in your steps, like so:</p> <div class=”highlight highlight-source-ruby“><pre><span class=”pl-c1“>When</span> <span class=”pl-sr“>/I sign in/</span> <span class=”pl-k“>do</span>

    within(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>#session<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) <span class="pl-k">do</span>
  fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Email<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>user@example.com<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
  fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">end</span>
click_button <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Sign in<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>You can switch to the Capybara.javascript_driver (:selenium by default) by tagging scenarios (or features) with @javascript:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-smi”>@javascript</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>Scenario:</span> <span class=“pl-k”>do</span> something <span class=“pl-c1”>Ajaxy</span>

    <span class="pl-c1">When</span> <span class="pl-c1">I</span> click the <span class="pl-c1">Ajax</span> link
...</pre></div>

    <p>There are also explicit tags for each registered driver set up for you (@selenium, @rack_test, etc).</p> <h2><a href=“#using-capybara-with-rspec” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-using-capybara-with-rspec”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-using-capybara-with-rspec”></a>Using Capybara with RSpec</h2> <p>Load RSpec 2+ support by adding the following line (typically to your spec_helper.rb file):</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-k”>require</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>capybara/rspec<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span></pre></div> <p>If you are using Rails, put your Capybara specs in spec/features (only works if <a href=“you”>www.relishapp.com/rspec/rspec-rails/docs/upgrade#file-type-inference-disabled“>you have it configured in RSpec</a>) and if you have your Capybara specs in a different directory, then tag the example groups with :type =&gt; :feature.</p> <p>If you are not using Rails, tag all the example groups in which you want to use Capybara with :type =&gt; :feature.</p> <p>You can now write your specs like so:</p> <div class=”highlight highlight-source-ruby“><pre>describe <span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>”</span>the signin process<span class=“pl-pds”>“</span></span>, <span class=”pl-c1“>:type</span> =&gt; <span class=”pl-c1“>:feature</span> <span class=”pl-k“>do</span>

    before <span class="pl-c1">:each</span> <span class="pl-k">do</span>
  <span class="pl-c1">User</span>.make(<span class="pl-c1">email:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>user@example.com<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">password:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

it <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>signs me in<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> <span class="pl-k">do</span>
  visit <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/sessions/new<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
  within(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>#session<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) <span class="pl-k">do</span>
    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Email<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>user@example.com<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
  <span class="pl-k">end</span>
  click_button <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Sign in<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
  expect(page).to have_content <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Success<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>Use js: true to switch to the Capybara.javascript_driver (:selenium by default), or provide a :driver option to switch to one specific driver. For example:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>describe <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>some stuff which requires js<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>, <span class=“pl-c1”>js:</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>true</span> <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    it <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>will use the default js driver<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
it <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>will switch to one specific driver<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">:driver</span> =&gt; <span class="pl-c1">:webkit</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>Capybara also comes with a built in DSL for creating descriptive acceptance tests:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>feature <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>Signing in<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span> <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    background <span class="pl-k">do</span>
  <span class="pl-c1">User</span>.make(<span class="pl-c1">email:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>user@example.com<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">password:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>caplin<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

scenario <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Signing in with correct credentials<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> <span class="pl-k">do</span>
  visit <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/sessions/new<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
  within(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>#session<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) <span class="pl-k">do</span>
    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Email<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>user@example.com<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>caplin<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
  <span class="pl-k">end</span>
  click_button <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Sign in<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
  expect(page).to have_content <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Success<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

given(<span class="pl-c1">:other_user</span>) { <span class="pl-c1">User</span>.make(<span class="pl-c1">email:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>other@example.com<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">password:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>rous<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) }

scenario <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Signing in as another user<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> <span class="pl-k">do</span>
  visit <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>/sessions/new<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
  within(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>#session<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) <span class="pl-k">do</span>
    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Email<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> other_user.email
    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> other_user.password
  <span class="pl-k">end</span>
  click_button <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Sign in<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
  expect(page).to have_content <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Invalid email or password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>feature is in fact just an alias for describe ..., :type =&gt; :feature, background is an alias for before, scenario for it, and given/given! aliases for let/let!, respectively.</p> <p>Finally, Capybara matchers are supported in view specs:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>RSpec</span>.describe <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>todos/show.html.erb<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>, <span class=“pl-c1”>type:</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>:view</span> <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    it <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>displays the todo title<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> <span class="pl-k">do</span>
  assign <span class="pl-c1">:todo</span>, <span class="pl-c1">Todo</span>.<span class="pl-k">new</span>(<span class="pl-c1">title:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Buy milk<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)

  render

  expect(rendered).to have_css(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>header h1<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">text:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Buy milk<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p><strong>Note: When you require 'capybara/rspec' proxy methods are installed to work around name collisions between Capybara::DSL methods all/within and the identically named built-in RSpec matchers. If you opt not to require 'capybara/rspec' you can install the proxy methods by requiring 'capybara/rspec/matcher_proxies' after requiring RSpec and 'capybara/dsl'</strong></p> <h2><a href=“#using-capybara-with-testunit” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-using-capybara-with-testunit”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-using-capybara-with-testunit”></a>Using Capybara with Test::Unit</h2> <ul> <li> <p>If you are using Test::Unit, define a base class for your Capybara tests like so:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-k”>require</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>capybara/dsl<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>class</span> <span class=“pl-en”>CapybaraTestCase<span class=“pl-e”> &lt; Test::Unit::TestCase</span></span>

    <span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>::<span class="pl-c1">DSL</span>

<span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">teardown</span>
  <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>.reset_sessions!
  <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>.use_default_driver
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> </li> </ul> <h2><a href=“#using-capybara-with-minitest” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-using-capybara-with-minitest”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-using-capybara-with-minitest”></a>Using Capybara with Minitest</h2> <ul> <li> <p>If you are using Rails, add the following code in your test_helper.rb file to make Capybara available in all test cases deriving from ActionDispatch::IntegrationTest:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-k”>require</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>capybara/rails<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span> <span class=“pl-k”>require</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>capybara/minitest<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>class</span> <span class=“pl-en”>ActionDispatch::IntegrationTest</span>

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Make the Capybara DSL available in all integration tests</span>
<span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>::<span class="pl-c1">DSL</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Make `assert_*` methods behave like Minitest assertions</span>
<span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>::<span class="pl-c1">Minitest</span>::<span class="pl-c1">Assertions</span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Reset sessions and driver between tests</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Use super wherever this method is redefined in your individual test classes</span>
<span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">teardown</span>
  <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>.reset_sessions!
  <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>.use_default_driver
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> </li> <li> <p>If you are not using Rails, define a base class for your Capybara tests like so:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-k”>require</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>capybara/minitest<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>class</span> <span class=“pl-en”>CapybaraTestCase<span class=“pl-e”> &lt; Minitest::Test</span></span>

    <span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>::<span class="pl-c1">DSL</span>
<span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>::<span class="pl-c1">Minitest</span>::<span class="pl-c1">Assertions</span>

<span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">teardown</span>
  <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>.reset_sessions!
  <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>.use_default_driver
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>Remember to call super in any subclasses that override teardown.</p> </li> </ul> <p>To switch the driver, set Capybara.current_driver. For instance,</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-k”>class</span> <span class=“pl-en”>BlogTest<span class=“pl-e”> &lt; ActionDispatch::IntegrationTest</span></span>

    setup <span class="pl-k">do</span>
  <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>.current_driver <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>.javascript_driver <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> :selenium by default</span>
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

<span class="pl-c1">test</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>shows blog posts<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span> <span class="pl-k">do</span>
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> ... this test is run with Selenium ...</span>
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <h2><a href=“#using-capybara-with-minitestspec” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-using-capybara-with-minitestspec”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-using-capybara-with-minitestspec”></a>Using Capybara with Minitest::Spec</h2> <p>Follow the above instructions for Minitest and additionally require capybara/minitest/spec</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>page.must_have_content(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Important!<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <h2><a href=“#drivers” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-drivers”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-drivers”></a>Drivers</h2> <p>Capybara uses the same DSL to drive a variety of browser and headless drivers.</p> <h3><a href=“#selecting-the-driver” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-selecting-the-driver”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-selecting-the-driver”></a>Selecting the Driver</h3> <p>By default, Capybara uses the :rack_test driver, which is fast but limited: it does not support JavaScript, nor is it able to access HTTP resources outside of your Rack application, such as remote APIs and OAuth services. To get around these limitations, you can set up a different default driver for your features. For example if you'd prefer to run everything in Selenium, you could do:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.default_driver <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>:selenium</span> <span class=“pl-c”><span class=“pl-c”>#</span> :selenium_chrome and :selenium_chrome_headless are also registered</span></pre></div> <p>However, if you are using RSpec or Cucumber, you may instead want to consider leaving the faster :rack_test as the <strong>default_driver</strong>, and marking only those tests that require a JavaScript-capable driver using js: true or @javascript, respectively. By default, JavaScript tests are run using the :selenium driver. You can change this by setting Capybara.javascript_driver.</p> <p>You can also change the driver temporarily (typically in the Before/setup and After/teardown blocks):</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.current_driver <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>:webkit</span> <span class=“pl-c”><span class=“pl-c”>#</span> temporarily select different driver</span> <span class=“pl-c”><span class=“pl-c”>#</span> tests here</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.use_default_driver <span class=“pl-c”><span class=“pl-c”>#</span> switch back to default driver</span></pre></div> <p><strong>Note</strong>: switching the driver creates a new session, so you may not be able to switch in the middle of a test.</p> <h3><a href=“#racktest” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-racktest”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-racktest”></a>RackTest</h3> <p>RackTest is Capybara's default driver. It is written in pure Ruby and does not have any support for executing JavaScript. Since the RackTest driver interacts directly with Rack interfaces, it does not require a server to be started. However, this means that if your application is not a Rack application (Rails, Sinatra and most other Ruby frameworks are Rack applications) then you cannot use this driver. Furthermore, you cannot use the RackTest driver to test a remote application, or to access remote URLs (e.g., redirects to external sites, external APIs, or OAuth services) that your application might interact with.</p> <p><a href=“capybara-mechanizegithub.com/jeroenvandijk/capybara-mechanize”>capybara-mechanize> provides a similar driver that can access remote servers.</p> <p>RackTest can be configured with a set of headers like this:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.register_driver <span class=“pl-c1”>:rack_test</span> <span class=“pl-k”>do</span> |<span class=“pl-smi”>app</span>|

    <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>::<span class="pl-c1">RackTest</span>::<span class="pl-c1">Driver</span>.<span class="pl-k">new</span>(app, <span class="pl-c1">headers:</span> { <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>HTTP_USER_AGENT<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span> =&gt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Capybara<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span> })

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>See the section on adding and configuring drivers.</p> <h3><a href=“#selenium” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-selenium”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-selenium”></a>Selenium</h3> <p>At the moment, Capybara supports <a href=“Selenium”>seleniumhq.org/docs/01_introducing_selenium.html#selenium-2-aka-selenium-webdriver“>Selenium 2.0+ (Webdriver)</a>, not Selenium RC. In order to use Selenium, you'll need to install the selenium-webdriver gem, and add it to your Gemfile if you're using bundler. Provided Firefox is installed, everything is set up for you, and you should be able to start using Selenium right away.</p> <p><strong>Note</strong>: drivers which run the server in a different thread may not share the same transaction as your tests, causing data not to be shared between your test and test server, see ”Transactions and database setup“ below.</p> <h3><a href=”#capybara-webkit“ aria-hidden=”true“ class=”anchor“ id=”user-content-capybara-webkit“><svg aria-hidden=”true“ class=”octicon octicon-link“ height=”16“ version=”1.1“ viewBox=”0 0 16 16“ width=”16“><path fill-rule=”evenodd“ d=”M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z“></path></svg></a><a name=”user-content-capybara-webkit“></a>Capybara-webkit</h3> <p>The <a href=”capybara-webkit“>github.com/thoughtbot/capybara-webkit”>capybara-webkit driver</a> is for true headless testing. It uses QtWebKit to start a rendering engine process. It can execute JavaScript as well. It is significantly faster than drivers like Selenium since it does not load an entire browser.</p> <p>You can install it with:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-shell”><pre>gem install capybara-webkit</pre></div> <p>And you can use it by:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.javascript_driver <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>:webkit</span></pre></div> <h3><a href=“#poltergeist” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-poltergeist”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-poltergeist”></a>Poltergeist</h3> <p><a href=“Poltergeistgithub.com/teampoltergeist/poltergeist”>Poltergeist> is another headless driver which integrates Capybara with <a href=“PhantomJSphantomjs.org/”>PhantomJS>. It is truly headless, so doesn't require Xvfb to run on your CI server. It will also detect and report any Javascript errors that happen within the page.</p> <h2><a href=“#the-dsl” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-the-dsl”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-the-dsl”></a>The DSL</h2> <p>A complete reference is available at <a href=“rubydoc.info.rubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/master”>rubydoc.info.> <p><strong>Note: By default Capybara will only locate visible elements. This is because a real user would not be able to interact with non-visible elements.</strong></p> <p><strong>Note</strong>: All searches in Capybara are case sensitive. This is because Capybara heavily uses XPath, which doesn't support case insensitivity.</p> <h3><a href=“#navigating” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-navigating”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-navigating”></a>Navigating</h3> <p>You can use the <a href="http://rubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/master/Capybara/Session#visit-instance_method">visit method to navigate to other pages:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>visit(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>/projects<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) visit(post_comments_path(post))</pre></div> <p>The visit method only takes a single parameter, the request method is <strong>always</strong> GET.</p> <p>You can get the <a href=“current”>rubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/master/Capybara/Session#current_path-instance_method“>current path</a> of the browsing session, and test it using the <a href=”have_current_pathwww.rubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/master/Capybara/RSpecMatchers#have_current_path-instance_method“>have_current_path> matcher:</p> <div class=”highlight highlight-source-ruby“><pre>expect(page).to have_current_path(post_comments_path(post))</pre></div> <p><strong>Note</strong>: You can also assert the current path by testing the value of current_path directly. However, using the have_current_path matcher is safer since it uses Capybara's <a href=”#asynchronous-javascript-ajax-and-friends“>waiting behaviour</a> to ensure that preceding actions (such as a click_link) have completed.</p> <h3><a href=”#clicking-links-and-buttons“ aria-hidden=”true“ class=”anchor“ id=”user-content-clicking-links-and-buttons“><svg aria-hidden=”true“ class=”octicon octicon-link“ height=”16“ version=”1.1“ viewBox=”0 0 16 16“ width=”16“><path fill-rule=”evenodd“ d=”M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z“></path></svg></a><a name=”user-content-clicking-links-and-buttons“></a>Clicking links and buttons</h3> <p>Full reference: <a href=”Capybara::Node::Actionsrubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/master/Capybara/Node/Actions“>Capybara::Node::Actions> <p>You can interact with the webapp by following links and buttons. Capybara automatically follows any redirects, and submits forms associated with buttons.</p> <div class=”highlight highlight-source-ruby“><pre>click_link(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>id-of-link<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>) click_link(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>Link Text<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>) click_button(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>Save<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>) click_on(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>Link Text<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>) <span class=”pl-c“><span class=”pl-c“>#</span> clicks on either links or buttons</span> click_on(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>Button Value<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <h3><a href=”#interacting-with-forms“ aria-hidden=”true“ class=”anchor“ id=”user-content-interacting-with-forms“><svg aria-hidden=”true“ class=”octicon octicon-link“ height=”16“ version=”1.1“ viewBox=”0 0 16 16“ width=”16“><path fill-rule=”evenodd“ d=”M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z“></path></svg></a><a name=”user-content-interacting-with-forms“></a>Interacting with forms</h3> <p>Full reference: <a href=”Capybara::Node::Actionsrubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/master/Capybara/Node/Actions“>Capybara::Node::Actions> <p>There are a number of tools for interacting with form elements:</p> <div class=”highlight highlight-source-ruby“><pre>fill_in(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>First Name<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>, <span class=”pl-c1“>with:</span> <span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>John<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>) fill_in(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>Password<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>, <span class=”pl-c1“>with:</span> <span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>Seekrit<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>) fill_in(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>Description<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>, <span class=”pl-c1“>with:</span> <span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>Really Long Text…<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>) choose(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>A Radio Button<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>) check(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>A Checkbox<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>) uncheck(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>A Checkbox<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>) attach_file(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>Image<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>, <span d=”M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 name=”user-content-querying“></a>Querying</h3> <p>Full reference: <a href=”Capybara::Node::Matchersrubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/master/Capybara/Node/Matchers“>Capybara::Node::Matchers> <p>Capybara has a rich set of options for querying the page for the existence of certain elements, and working with and manipulating those elements.</p> <div class=”highlight highlight-source-ruby“><pre>page.has_selector?(<span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>table tr<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>) page.has_selector?(<span class=”pl-c1“>:xpath</span>, <span class=”pl-s“><span class=”pl-pds“>'</span>.//table/tr<span class=”pl-pds“>'</span></span>)

    page.has_xpath?(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>.//table/tr<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) page.has_css?(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>table tr.foo<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) page.has_content?(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>foo<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <p><strong>Note:</strong> The negative forms like has_no_selector? are different from not has_selector?. Read the section on asynchronous JavaScript for an explanation.</p> <p>You can use these with RSpec's magic matchers:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>expect(page).to have_selector(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>table tr<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) expect(page).to have_selector(<span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>.//table/tr<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)

    expect(page).to have_xpath(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>.//table/tr<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) expect(page).to have_css(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>table tr.foo<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) expect(page).to have_content(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>foo<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <h3><a href=“#finding” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-finding”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-finding”></a>Finding</h3> <p>Full reference: <a href=“Capybara::Node::Findersrubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/master/Capybara/Node/Finders”>Capybara::Node::Finders> <p>You can also find specific elements, in order to manipulate them:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>find_field(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>First Name<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).value find_field(<span class=“pl-c1”>id:</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>my_field<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).value find_link(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Hello<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>, <span class=“pl-c1”>:visible</span> =&gt; <span class=“pl-c1”>:all</span>).visible? find_link(<span class=“pl-c1”>class:</span> [<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>some_class<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>some_other_class<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>], <span class=“pl-c1”>:visible</span> =&gt; <span class=“pl-c1”>:all</span>).visible?

    find_button(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Send<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).click find_button(<span class=“pl-c1”>value:</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>1234<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).click

    find(<span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>.//table/tr<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>).click find(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>#overlay<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>).find(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>h1<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>).click all(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>a<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).each { |<span class=“pl-smi”>a</span>| a[<span class=“pl-c1”>:href</span>] }</pre></div> <p>If you need to find elements by additional attributes/properties you can also pass a filter block, which will be checked inside the normal waiting behavior. If you find yourself needing to use this a lot you may be better off adding a <a href=“custom”>www.rubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/Capybara#add_selector-class_method“>custom selector</a> or <a href=”adding“>www.rubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/Capybara#modify_selector-class_method”>adding a filter to an existing selector</a>.</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>find_field(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>First Name<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>){ |<span class=“pl-smi”>el</span>| el[<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>data-xyz<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>] <span class=“pl-k”>==</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>123<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span> } find(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>#img_loading<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>){ |<span class=“pl-smi”>img</span>| img[<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>complete<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>] <span class=“pl-k”>==</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>true</span> }</pre></div> <p><strong>Note</strong>: find will wait for an element to appear on the page, as explained in the Ajax section. If the element does not appear it will raise an error.</p> <p>These elements all have all the Capybara DSL methods available, so you can restrict them to specific parts of the page:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>find(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>#navigation<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).click_link(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Home<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) expect(find(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>#navigation<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)).to have_button(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Sign out<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <h3><a href=“#scoping” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-scoping”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-scoping”></a>Scoping</h3> <p>Capybara makes it possible to restrict certain actions, such as interacting with forms or clicking links and buttons, to within a specific area of the page. For this purpose you can use the generic <a href="http://rubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/master/Capybara/Session#within-instance_method">within method. Optionally you can specify which kind of selector to use.</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>within(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>li#employee<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Name<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Jimmy<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span>

    within(<span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“.//li<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Name<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Jimmy<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>There are special methods for restricting the scope to a specific fieldset, identified by either an id or the text of the fieldset's legend tag, and to a specific table, identified by either id or text of the table's caption tag.</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>within_fieldset(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Employee<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Name<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Jimmy<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span>

    within_table(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Employee<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Name<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Jimmy<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <h3><a href=“#working-with-windows” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-working-with-windows”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-working-with-windows”></a>Working with windows</h3> <p>Capybara provides some methods to ease finding and switching windows:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>facebook_window <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> window_opened_by <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    click_button <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Like<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span> within_window facebook_window <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    find(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>#login_email<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>).set(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>a@example.com<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
find(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>#login_password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>).set(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>qwerty<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
