    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <h3><a href=“#scripting” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-scripting”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-scripting”></a>Scripting</h3> <p>In drivers which support it, you can easily execute JavaScript:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>page.execute_script(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>$('body').empty()<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>)</pre></div> <p>For simple expressions, you can return the result of the script. Note that this may break with more complicated expressions:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>result <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> page.evaluate_script(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>4 + 4<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>);</pre></div> <h3><a href=“#modals” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-modals”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-modals”></a>Modals</h3> <p>In drivers which support it, you can accept, dismiss and respond to alerts, confirms and prompts.</p> <p>You can accept or dismiss alert messages by wrapping the code that produces an alert in a block:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>accept_alert <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    click_link(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Show Alert<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>You can accept or dismiss a confirmation by wrapping it in a block, as well:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>dismiss_confirm <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    click_link(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Show Confirm<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>You can accept or dismiss prompts as well, and also provide text to fill in for the response:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>accept_prompt(<span class=“pl-c1”>with:</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Linus Torvalds<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    click_link(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Show Prompt About Linux<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>All modal methods return the message that was presented. So, you can access the prompt message by assigning the return to a variable:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>message <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> accept_prompt(<span class=“pl-c1”>with:</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Linus Torvalds<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    click_link(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Show Prompt About Linux<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span> expect(message).to eq(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Who is the chief architect of Linux?<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <h3><a href=“#debugging” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-debugging”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-debugging”></a>Debugging</h3> <p>It can be useful to take a snapshot of the page as it currently is and take a look at it:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>save_and_open_page</pre></div> <p>You can also retrieve the current state of the DOM as a string using <a href="http://rubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/master/Capybara/Session#html-instance_method">page.html.> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>print</span> page.html</pre></div> <p>This is mostly useful for debugging. You should avoid testing against the contents of page.html and use the more expressive finder methods instead.</p> <p>Finally, in drivers that support it, you can save a screenshot:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>page.save_screenshot(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>screenshot.png<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <p>Or have it save and automatically open:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>save_and_open_screenshot</pre></div> <p>Screenshots are saved to Capybara.save_path, relative to the app directory. If you have required capybara/rails, Capybara.save_path will default to tmp/capybara.</p> <h2><a href=“#matching” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-matching”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-matching”></a>Matching</h2> <p>It is possible to customize how Capybara finds elements. At your disposal are two options, Capybara.exact and Capybara.match.</p> <h3><a href=“#exactness” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-exactness”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-exactness”></a>Exactness</h3> <p>Capybara.exact and the exact option work together with the is expression inside the XPath gem. When exact is true, all is expressions match exactly, when it is false, they allow substring matches. Many of the selectors built into Capybara use the is expression. This way you can specify whether you want to allow substring matches or not. Capybara.exact is false by default.</p> <p>For example:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>click_link(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>Password<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>) <span class=“pl-c”><span class=“pl-c”>#</span> also matches “Password confirmation”</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.exact <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>true</span> click_link(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>Password<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>) <span class=“pl-c”><span class=“pl-c”>#</span> does not match “Password confirmation”</span> click_link(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>Password<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>, <span class=“pl-c1”>exact:</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>false</span>) <span class=“pl-c”><span class=“pl-c”>#</span> can be overridden</span></pre></div> <h3><a href=“#strategy” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-strategy”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-strategy”></a>Strategy</h3> <p>Using Capybara.match and the equivalent match option, you can control how Capybara behaves when multiple elements all match a query. There are currently four different strategies built into Capybara:</p> <ol> <li><strong>first:</strong> Just picks the first element that matches.</li> <li><strong>one:</strong> Raises an error if more than one element matches.</li> <li><strong>smart:</strong> If exact is true, raises an error if more than one element matches, just like one. If exact is false, it will first try to find an exact match. An error is raised if more than one element is found. If no element is found, a new search is performed which allows partial matches. If that search returns multiple matches, an error is raised.</li> <li><strong>prefer_exact:</strong> If multiple matches are found, some of which are exact, and some of which are not, then the first exactly matching element is returned.</li> </ol> <p>The default for Capybara.match is :smart. To emulate the behaviour in Capybara 2.0.x, set Capybara.match to :one. To emulate the behaviour in Capybara 1.x, set Capybara.match to :prefer_exact.</p> <h2><a href=“#transactions-and-database-setup” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-transactions-and-database-setup”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-transactions-and-database-setup”></a>Transactions and database setup</h2> <p><strong>Note:</strong> Rails 5.1+ now “safely” shares the database connection between the app and test threads. Therefore, if using Rails 5.1+ you SHOULD be able to ignore this section.</p> <p>Some Capybara drivers need to run against an actual HTTP server. Capybara takes care of this and starts one for you in the same process as your test, but on another thread. Selenium is one of those drivers, whereas RackTest is not.</p> <p>If you are using a SQL database, it is common to run every test in a transaction, which is rolled back at the end of the test, rspec-rails does this by default out of the box for example. Since transactions are usually not shared across threads, this will cause data you have put into the database in your test code to be invisible to Capybara.</p> <p>Cucumber handles this by using truncation instead of transactions, i.e. they empty out the entire database after each test. You can get the same behaviour by using a gem such as <a href=“database_cleaner.github.com/DatabaseCleaner/database_cleaner”>database_cleaner.> <h2><a href=“#asynchronous-javascript-ajax-and-friends” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-asynchronous-javascript-ajax-and-friends”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-asynchronous-javascript-ajax-and-friends”></a>Asynchronous JavaScript (Ajax and friends)</h2> <p>When working with asynchronous JavaScript, you might come across situations where you are attempting to interact with an element which is not yet present on the page. Capybara automatically deals with this by waiting for elements to appear on the page.</p> <p>When issuing instructions to the DSL such as:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>click_link(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>foo<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) click_link(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>bar<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) expect(page).to have_content(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>baz<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <p>If clicking on the foo link triggers an asynchronous process, such as an Ajax request, which, when complete will add the bar link to the page, clicking on the bar link would be expected to fail, since that link doesn't exist yet. However Capybara is smart enough to retry finding the link for a brief period of time before giving up and throwing an error. The same is true of the next line, which looks for the content baz on the page; it will retry looking for that content for a brief time. You can adjust how long this period is (the default is 2 seconds):</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.default_max_wait_time <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>5</span></pre></div> <p>Be aware that because of this behaviour, the following two statements are <strong>not</strong> equivalent, and you should <strong>always</strong> use the latter!</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-k”>!</span>page.has_xpath?(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>a<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) page.has_no_xpath?(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>a<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <p>The former would immediately fail because the content has not yet been removed. Only the latter would wait for the asynchronous process to remove the content from the page.</p> <p>Capybara's RSpec matchers, however, are smart enough to handle either form. The two following statements are functionally equivalent:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>expect(page).not_to have_xpath(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>a<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) expect(page).to have_no_xpath(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>a<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <p>Capybara's waiting behaviour is quite advanced, and can deal with situations such as the following line of code:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>expect(find(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>#sidebar<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).find(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>h1<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)).to have_content(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Something<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <p>Even if JavaScript causes #sidebar to disappear off the page, Capybara will automatically reload it and any elements it contains. So if an AJAX request causes the contents of #sidebar to change, which would update the text of the h1 to “Something”, and this happened, this test would pass. If you do not want this behaviour, you can set Capybara.automatic_reload to false.</p> <h2><a href=“#using-the-dsl-elsewhere” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-using-the-dsl-elsewhere”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-using-the-dsl-elsewhere”></a>Using the DSL elsewhere</h2> <p>You can mix the DSL into any context by including Capybara::DSL:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-k”>require</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>capybara/dsl<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>

    <span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.default_driver <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>:webkit</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>module</span> <span class=“pl-en”>MyModule</span>

    <span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>::<span class="pl-c1">DSL</span>

<span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">login!</span>
  within(<span class="pl-c1">:xpath</span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>.//form[@id='session']<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) <span class="pl-k">do</span>
    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Email<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>user@example.com<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
    fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
  <span class="pl-k">end</span>
  click_button <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Sign in<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>This enables its use in unsupported testing frameworks, and for general-purpose scripting.</p> <h2><a href=“#calling-remote-servers” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-calling-remote-servers”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-calling-remote-servers”></a>Calling remote servers</h2> <p>Normally Capybara expects to be testing an in-process Rack application, but you can also use it to talk to a web server running anywhere on the internet, by setting app_host:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.current_driver <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>:selenium</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.app_host <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>www.google.com class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span> … visit(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>/<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <p><strong>Note</strong>: the default driver (:rack_test) does not support running against a remote server. With drivers that support it, you can also visit any URL directly:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>visit(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>www.google.com class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <p>By default Capybara will try to boot a rack application automatically. You might want to switch off Capybara's rack server if you are running against a remote application:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.run_server <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>false</span></pre></div> <h2><a href=“#using-sessions” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-using-sessions”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-using-sessions”></a>Using sessions</h2> <p>Capybara manages named sessions (:default if not specified) allowing multiple sessions using the same driver and test app instance to be interacted with. A new session will be created using the current driver if a session with the given name using the current driver and test app instance is not found.</p> <h3><a href=“#named-sessions” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-named-sessions”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a>Named sessions</h3> <p>To perform operations in a different session and then revert to the previous session</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.using_session(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>Bob's session<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>do something in Bob's browser session</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span>

    <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span>reverts to previous session</span></pre></div>

    <p>To permanently switch the current session to a different session</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.session_name <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>some other session<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span></pre></div> <h3><a href=“#using-sessions-manually” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-using-sessions-manually”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-using-sessions-manually”></a>Using sessions manually</h3> <p>For ultimate control, you can instantiate and use a <a href=“Sessionrubydoc.info/github/teamcapybara/capybara/master/Capybara/Session”>Session> manually.</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-k”>require</span> <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>capybara<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>

    session <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>::<span class=“pl-c1”>Session</span>.<span class=“pl-k”>new</span>(<span class=“pl-c1”>:webkit</span>, my_rack_app) session.within(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>“</span>form#session<span class=”pl-pds“>”</span></span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    session.fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Email<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>user@example.com<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
session.fill_in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">with:</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>password<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span> session.click_button <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>Sign in<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span></pre></div> <h2><a href=“#xpath-css-and-selectors” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-xpath-css-and-selectors”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-xpath-css-and-selectors”></a>XPath, CSS and selectors</h2> <p>Capybara does not try to guess what kind of selector you are going to give it, and will always use CSS by default. If you want to use XPath, you'll need to do:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>within(<span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>.//ul/li<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) { … } find(<span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>.//ul/li<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).text find(<span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>.//li[contains(.//a[@href = “#”]/text(), “foo”)]<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).value</pre></div> <p>Alternatively you can set the default selector to XPath:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.default_selector <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span> find(<span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>.//ul/li<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).text</pre></div> <p>Capybara allows you to add custom selectors, which can be very useful if you find yourself using the same kinds of selectors very often:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.add_selector(<span class=“pl-c1”>:id</span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    xpath { |<span class="pl-smi">id</span>| <span class="pl-c1">XPath</span>.descendant[<span class="pl-c1">XPath</span>.<span class="pl-k">attr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">:id</span>) <span class="pl-k">==</span> id.to_s] }

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span>

    <span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.add_selector(<span class=“pl-c1”>:row</span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    xpath { |<span class="pl-smi">num</span>| <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>.//tbody/tr[<span class="pl-pse">#{</span><span class="pl-s1">num</span><span class="pl-pse">}</span>]<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> }

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span>

    <span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.add_selector(<span class=“pl-c1”>:flash_type</span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    css { |<span class="pl-smi">type</span>| <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>#flash.<span class="pl-pse">#{</span><span class="pl-s1">type</span><span class="pl-pse">}</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> }

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>The block given to xpath must always return an XPath expression as a String, or an XPath expression generated through the XPath gem. You can now use these selectors like this:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>find(<span class=“pl-c1”>:id</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>post_123<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) find(<span class=“pl-c1”>:row</span>, <span class=“pl-c1”>3</span>) find(<span class=“pl-c1”>:flash_type</span>, <span class=“pl-c1”>:notice</span>)</pre></div> <h2><a href=“#beware-the-xpath–trap” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-beware-the-xpath–trap”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-beware-the-xpath–trap”></a>Beware the XPath // trap</h2> <p>In XPath the expression // means something very specific, and it might not be what you think. Contrary to common belief, // means “anywhere in the document” not “anywhere in the current context”. As an example:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>page.find(<span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>//body<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).all(<span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>//script<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <p>You might expect this to find all script tags in the body, but actually, it finds all script tags in the entire document, not only those in the body! What you're looking for is the .// expression which means “any descendant of the current node”:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>page.find(<span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>//body<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>).all(<span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>.//script<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>)</pre></div> <p>The same thing goes for within:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre>within(<span class=“pl-c1”>:xpath</span>, <span class=“pl-s”><span class=“pl-pds”>'</span>//body<span class=“pl-pds”>'</span></span>) <span class=“pl-k”>do</span>

    page.find(<span class="pl-c1">:xpath</span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>.//script<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>)
within(<span class="pl-c1">:xpath</span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>.//table/tbody<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) <span class="pl-k">do</span>
...
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <h2><a href=“#configuring-and-adding-drivers” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-configuring-and-adding-drivers”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-configuring-and-adding-drivers”></a>Configuring and adding drivers</h2> <p>Capybara makes it convenient to switch between different drivers. It also exposes an API to tweak those drivers with whatever settings you want, or to add your own drivers. This is how to override the selenium driver configuration to use chrome:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.register_driver <span class=“pl-c1”>:selenium</span> <span class=“pl-k”>do</span> |<span class=“pl-smi”>app</span>|

    <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>::<span class="pl-c1">Selenium</span>::<span class="pl-c1">Driver</span>.<span class="pl-k">new</span>(app, <span class="pl-c1">:browser</span> =&gt; <span class="pl-c1">:chrome</span>)

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>However, it's also possible to give this configuration a different name.</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.register_driver <span class=“pl-c1”>:selenium_chrome</span> <span class=“pl-k”>do</span> |<span class=“pl-smi”>app</span>|

    <span class="pl-c1">Capybara</span>::<span class="pl-c1">Selenium</span>::<span class="pl-c1">Driver</span>.<span class="pl-k">new</span>(app, <span class="pl-c1">:browser</span> =&gt; <span class="pl-c1">:chrome</span>)

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span></pre></div> <p>Then tests can switch between using different browsers effortlessly:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-ruby”><pre><span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.current_driver <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>:selenium_chrome</span></pre></div> <p>Whatever is returned from the block should conform to the API described by Capybara::Driver::Base, it does not however have to inherit from this class. Gems can use this API to add their own drivers to Capybara.</p> <p>The <a href=“Selenium”>github.com/SeleniumHQ/selenium/wiki/Ruby-Bindings“>Selenium wiki</a> has additional info about how the underlying driver can be configured.</p> <h2><a href=”#gotchas“ aria-hidden=”true“ class=”anchor“ id=”user-content-gotchas“><svg aria-hidden=”true“ class=”octicon octicon-link“ height=”16“ version=”1.1“ viewBox=”0 0 16 16“ width=”16“><path fill-rule=”evenodd“ d=”M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z“></path></svg></a><a name=”user-content-gotchas“></a>Gotchas:</h2> <ul> <li> <p>Access to session and request is not possible from the test, Access to response is limited. Some drivers allow access to response headers and HTTP status code, but this kind of functionality is not provided by some drivers, such as Selenium.</p> </li> <li> <p>Access to Rails specific stuff (such as controller) is unavailable, since we're not using Rails' integration testing.</p> </li> <li> <p>Freezing time: It's common practice to mock out the Time so that features that depend on the current Date work as expected. This can be problematic on ruby/platform combinations that don't support access to a monotonic process clock, since Capybara's Ajax timing uses the system time, resulting in Capybara never timing out and just hanging when a failure occurs. It's still possible to use gems which allow you to travel in time, rather than freeze time. One such gem is <a href=”Timecop.github.com/travisjeffery/timecop“>Timecop.> </li> <li> <p>When using Rack::Test, beware if attempting to visit absolute URLs. For example, a session might not be shared between visits to posts_path and posts_url. If testing an absolute URL in an Action Mailer email, set default_url_options to match the Rails default of www.example.com.> </li> <li> <p>Server errors will only be raised in the session that initiates the server thread. If you are testing for specific server errors and using multiple sessions make sure to test for the errors using the initial session (usually :default)</p> </li> </ul> <h2><a href=”#threadsafe-mode—beta—may-change“ aria-hidden=”true“ class=”anchor“ id=”user-content-threadsafe-mode—beta—may-change“><svg aria-hidden=”true“ class=”octicon octicon-link“ height=”16“ version=”1.1“ viewBox=”0 0 16 16“ width=”16“><path fill-rule=”evenodd“ d=”M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z“></path></svg></a><a name=”user-content-threadsafe“></a>”Threadsafe“ mode - BETA - may change</h2> <p>In normal mode most of Capybara's configuration options are global settings which can cause issues if using multiple sessions and wanting to change a setting for only one of the sessions. To provide support for this type of usage Capybara now provides a ”threadsafe“ mode which can be enabled by setting</p> <div class=”highlight highlight-source-ruby“><pre><span class=”pl-c1“>Capybara</span>.threadsafe <span class=”pl-k“>=</span> <span class=”pl-c1“>true</span></pre></div> <p>This setting can only be changed before any sessions have been created. In ”threadsafe“ mode the following behaviors of Capybara change</p> <ul> <li> <p>Most options can now be set on a session. These can either be set at session creation time or after, and default to the global options at the time of session creation. Options which are NOT session specific are app, reuse_server, default_driver, javascript_driver, and (obviously) threadsafe. Any drivers and servers registered through register_driver and register_server are also global.</p> <div class=”highlight highlight-source-ruby“><pre>my_session <span class=”pl-k“>=</span> <span class=”pl-c1“>Capybara</span>::<span class=”pl-c1“>Session</span>.<span class=”pl-k“>new</span>(<span class=”pl-c1“>:driver</span>, some_app) <span class=”pl-k“>do</span> |<span class=”pl-smi“>config</span>|

    config.automatic_label_click <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">true</span> <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> only set for my_session</span>

    <span class=“pl-k”>end</span> my_session.config.default_max_wait_time <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>10</span> <span class=“pl-c”><span class=“pl-c”>#</span> only set for my_session</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>Capybara</span>.default_max_wait_time <span class=“pl-k”>=</span> <span class=“pl-c1”>2</span> <span class=“pl-c”><span class=“pl-c”>#</span> will not change the default_max_wait in my_session</span></pre></div> </li> <li> <p>current_driver and session_name are thread specific. This means that using_session and using_driver also only affect the current thread.</p> </li> </ul> <h2><a href=“#development” aria-hidden=“true” class=“anchor” id=“user-content-development”><svg aria-hidden=“true” class=“octicon octicon-link” height=“16” version=“1.1” viewBox=“0 0 16 16” width=“16”><path fill-rule=“evenodd” d=“M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z”></path></svg></a><a name=“user-content-development”></a>Development</h2> <p>To set up a development environment, simply do:</p> <div class=“highlight highlight-source-shell”><pre>bundle install bundle <span class=“pl-c1”>exec</span> rake <span class=“pl-c”><span class=“pl-c”>#</span> run the test suite</span></pre></div> <p>See <a href=“CONTRIBUTING.mdgithub.com/teamcapybara/capybara/blob/master/CONTRIBUTING.md”>CONTRIBUTING.md> for how to send issues and pull requests.</p> </article>

    </div>
